**Question 632:** MISTAKE: "Direct and inverse proportion always linear"
**Options:**

B) Inverse y=k/x is NOT linear (hyperbola)
C) Both A and B
D) Both are always linear

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Proportions
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Graph shape difference. Direct proportion y=kx is linear (straight line), but inverse proportion y=k/x is a hyperbola (not linear). Both A and B correctly explain the difference.

**Question 633:** ERROR: "If 5 workers take 20 days, 10 workers take 10 days (half workers=double time)"

A) WRONG! 10 workers take 10 days (inverse: more workers = less time)

C) Both A and B
D) More workers always take more time

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Proportions
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Inverse proportion directionality. For inverse proportion, more workers result in less time. Using 5 √ó 20 = 10 √ó d gives d = 10 days. Both A and B correctly explain inverse proportion.

**Question 634:** MISCONCEPTION: "Proportion requires k to be integer"

**Topic:** Proportions

**Question 635:** ERROR: "If y‚àùx and y‚àùz, then y‚àùx+z"
**Options:**
A) WRONG! If y‚àùx and y‚àùz separately, relationship is complex
B) Could be y‚àùxz (combined) or y‚àùx/z (mixed)
C) Both A and B
D) This relationship correct

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Proportions
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Multi-variable proportion care needed. When y is proportional to multiple variables, the relationship could be y‚àùxz (multiplicative) or y‚àùx/z (mixed), not y‚àùx+z (additive). Both A and B correctly identify the error.

**Question 691:** "In partnership, why wage distribution ‚àù work done, not time?"
**Options:**
A) Two workers same time, unequal efficiency ‚Üí unequal wage
B) Work done = quantity, not time quantity
C) Both A and B
D) Fair distribution requires proportional wage

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Fair wage principle. Wage should be proportional to work done, not just time, because workers with different efficiencies do different amounts of work in the same time. All statements are correct.

**Question 694:** "Real-world proportions rarely pure (y=kx). Why?"
**Options:**
A) Multiple variables interact
B) Saturation/constraints apply
C) Model limitations vs. reality
D) All above explain

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Proportions
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Real-world complexity. Pure proportions (y=kx) are simplified models. Reality involves multiple interacting variables, saturation effects, and constraints that limit pure proportional relationships. All statements explain why real-world proportions are rarely pure.

**Question 701:** A completes in 10 days (efficiency 80%), B in 12 days (efficiency 100%). Together real time?
**Options:**
A) A's effective rate = 0.8 √ó 1/10 = 0.08
B) B's effective rate = 1/12 ‚âà 0.083
C) Combined ‚âà 0.163 per day ‚Üí ~6.1 days
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 5
**Explanation:** Efficiency-adjusted work rate. A's effective rate = 0.08, B's effective rate ‚âà 0.083, combined ‚âà 0.163, so time together ‚âà 6.1 days. All calculations are correct.

---

D) All above

**Day:** 5
**Explanation:** Sequential work on multiple jobs. A completes 0.5 job, remaining 1.5 jobs for B = 22.5 days. Both calculations are correct.

**Question 708:** Pipe problem: A fills in 4 hours. After 1 hour, drain opens. Tank fills in 2 more hours total. Drain rate?
**Options:**
A) A fills 1 hour = 1/4 tank
B) Remaining = 3/4, done in 2 hours with both open
C) Net rate = 3/4 √∑ 2 = 3/8 per hour
D) Drain = 1/4 - 3/8 = -1/8 per hour (empties)

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 3
**Day:** 5
**Explanation:** Finding drain rate from phased filling. A fills 1/4 in 1 hour, remaining 3/4 filled in 2 hours with both open, so net rate = 3/8, drain rate = 1/8 per hour. All calculations are correct.

**Question 751:** What does "worker-days" measure?
**Options:**
A) Total effort required = workers √ó days
B) Example: 10 workers √ó 20 days = 200 worker-days total
C) Universal metric independent of team size
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Worker-days is a universal metric that measures total effort. It equals workers √ó days, providing a consistent measure regardless of team size. Example: 10 workers √ó 20 days = 200 worker-days. All statements are correct.

---

**Question 752:** Project needs 240 worker-days. How many days for 12 workers?
**Options:**
A) Days = 240 / 12 = 20 days
B) Both A above
C) All above

**Answer:** A
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Using worker-days formula: Days = Total worker-days / Workers = 240 / 12 = 20 days. This demonstrates the inverse relationship between workers and days for fixed total effort.

---

**Question 753:** 8 workers, 30 days planned. How many worker-days total?
**Options:**
A) 8 √ó 30 = 240 worker-days
B) This is the fixed total effort needed
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Total worker-days = 8 √ó 30 = 240. This represents the fixed total effort required for the project, independent of how the work is distributed. All statements are correct.

---

**Question 754:** If 10 workers complete in 25 days, how long for 20 workers?

D) All above

**Difficulty:** Easy

**Question 765:** INTERVIEW: Diminishing returns with hiring. Each additional worker saves how much time?

C) Both A and B

**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Hiring additional workers does not provide linear time savings. The first worker may save significant time, but subsequent workers provide diminishing returns, especially when hired late in the project. This follows the law of diminishing returns in scaling. Both A and B are correct.

**Question 766:** Worker A normally takes 10 days (rate 1/10). 50% efficiency boost. New time?

**Answer:** D

**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 1

**Question 772:** A works alone 3 days (rate 1/10), then B joins (rate 1/15), work 4 days together. A leaves, B finishes.
**Options:**
A) A's 3 days = 3/10, AB's 4 days = 4(1/10 + 1/15) = 4(5/30) = 2/3
B) Total so far = 3/10 + 2/3 = 9/30 + 20/30 = 29/30
C) Remaining = 1/30 for B alone = (1/30) / (1/15) = 0.5 days
D) Total ‚âà 7.5 days

**Explanation:** Interview tip: state fairness principle upfront ("fair profit = proportional to contribution"), define contribution clearly (capital, labor, or both), and show transparent calculations. All steps demonstrate professional problem-solving approach.

## DAY 3: PIPES FUNDAMENTALS (Q851-Q900)

**Question 851:** Pipe A fills tank in 6 hours. Rate?
**Options:**
A) 1/6 tank per hour
B) In 4 hours fill 4/6 = 2/3 tank
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Pipe filling rate = 1/6 tank per hour. In 4 hours, fills 2/3 tank. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 852:** Pipe A fills 6 hours, B fills 9 hours. Together?
**Options:**
A) Rate A = 1/6, Rate B = 1/9
B) Combined = 1/6 + 1/9 = 5/18 per hour
C) Time = 18/5 = 3.6 hours
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Combined rate = 5/18 per hour, so time = 3.6 hours. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 853:** Two pipes: combined 4 hours. Pipe A alone 6 hours. Pipe B alone?
**Options:**
A) Combined 1/4, A = 1/6
B) B = 1/4 - 1/6 = 1/12
C) B alone = 12 hours
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Combined rate = 1/4, A's rate = 1/6, so B's rate = 1/12, B alone = 12 hours. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 854:** Three pipes: 1/8, 1/12, 1/16 per hour. Combined time?
**Options:**
A) Combined = 1/8 + 1/12 + 1/16 = 13/48
B) Time = 48/13 ‚âà 3.69 hours
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Combined rate = 13/48 per hour, so time ‚âà 3.69 hours. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 855:** Pipe A fills 1/10 per hour. In 5 hours, how much filled?
**Options:**
A) 5 √ó 1/10 = 1/2 tank
B) Remaining = 1/2
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** In 5 hours, fills 1/2 tank, remaining = 1/2. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 856:** Tank 3/4 full. Pipe fills 1/6 per hour. Time to fill?

A) Remaining = 1/4
B) Rate = 1/6, Time = (1/4) / (1/6) = 1.5 hours
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Remaining = 1/4, rate = 1/6 per hour, so time = 1.5 hours. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 857:** Two pipes: A (1/8), B (1/12). B open 2 hours, then A joins. Total time?
**Options:**
A) B's 2 hours = 2/12 = 1/6 tank
B) Remaining = 5/6, Combined = 1/8 + 1/12 = 5/24
C) Time for remaining = (5/6) / (5/24) = 4 hours
D) Total = 6 hours

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Phase 1: B fills 1/6 in 2 hours. Remaining = 5/6. Combined rate = 5/24 per hour, so remaining takes 4 hours. Total = 6 hours. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 858:** Three pipes open 3 hours fill 1/2 tank. One pipe's rate?
**Options:**
A) Combined rate √ó 3 = 1/2
B) Combined = 1/6 per hour

D) Depends on individual pipe info

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Combined rate = 1/6 per hour. If pipes are equal, each = 1/18 per hour. However, individual pipe rates depend on specific information provided. Option D correctly identifies the need for individual pipe data.

---

**Question 859:** Pipe A faster than B. Together 5 hours. A alone 8 hours. B alone?

B) B = 1/5 - 1/8 = 3/40

D) All above

**Topic:** Time & Work

---

**Question 860:** INTERVIEW: Four pipes. If 3 fill in 6 hours, and 4th is drain (empties in 8 hours), combined time?
**Options:**
A) Three inlets combined: unclear individual rates
B) Assuming equal inlets: each 1/18, combined 3/18 = 1/6
C) With drain 1/8: net = 1/6 - 1/8 = 1/24 per hour
D) Time = 24 hours (must clarify individual pipe info)

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** If three equal inlets fill in 6 hours, each = 1/18, combined = 1/6. With drain 1/8, net = 1/24 per hour, time = 24 hours. However, individual pipe information must be clarified. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 861:** Pipe A fills 1/6 tank/hour. Drain empties 1/10 tank/hour. Both open. Net?
**Options:**
A) Net = 1/6 - 1/10 = 1/15 per hour
B) Time to fill = 15 hours
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Net rate = 1/15 per hour, so time to fill = 15 hours. Both calculations are correct.

**Question 867:** Leak develops: was filling in 8 hours with inlet. Now takes 12 hours. Leak rate?

**Question 868:** Tank drains due to large leak. Inlet 1/10, leak 1/6. Will it ever fill?
**Options:**

D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Net rate = -1/15 (negative), so tank cannot fill. To fill, must either close leak or increase inlet rate. All statements are correct.

---

**Question 869:** Leaky tank: inlet 1/5, leak (constant) 1/10. After 2 hours, leak fixed. Total time?
**Options:**
A) Phase 1 net = 1/5 - 1/10 = 1/10 per hour, work = 2/10 = 1/5
B) Phase 2 remaining = 4/5, rate = 1/5, time = 4 hours
C) Total = 6 hours
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Phase 1: net rate = 1/10 per hour, fills 1/5 in 2 hours. Phase 2: remaining = 4/5, rate = 1/5 per hour, takes 4 hours. Total = 6 hours. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 870:** INTERVIEW: Real scenario - swimming pool. Two inlets, one drain. Total time formula?
**Options:**
A) Time = 1 / (inlet1 + inlet2 - drain)
B) All rates must be positive (inlets) or negative (drain)
C) Both A and B (with explanation of sign convention)
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Time = 1 / (inlet1 + inlet2 - drain). Inlet rates are positive, drain rate is negative (subtracted). Both A and B correctly explain the formula and sign convention.

---

**Question 871:** Pipe A fills 1/8, B fills 1/12. A open 2 hours, then B joins. Time for B to fill remaining?
**Options:**
A) A does 2/8 = 1/4, remaining 3/4
B) AB rate = 5/24, time = 18/5 = 3.6 hours total
C) Total time = 2 + 3.6 = 5.6 hours
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Phase 1: A fills 1/4 in 2 hours. Remaining = 3/4. Phase 2: Combined rate = 5/24 per hour, takes 3.6 hours. Total = 5.6 hours. All calculations are correct.

A) Per cycle: 2/6 + 3/8 = 13/24 tank

**Question 874:** Two fill pipes and two drains all open. Rate calculations?
**Options:**

C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Net rate = sum of all inlet rates minus sum of all drain rates. Both A and B correctly describe the calculation method.

## DAY 4: PIPES ADVANCED & COMPLEX (Q901-Q950)

**Question 901:** Leak develops mid-filling: Inlet 1/10/hr. After 3 hours (3/10 tank), leak 1/15/hr opens. Time to fill?
**Options:**
A) Phase 1: 3 hours at 1/10, fill 3/10 tank
B) Remaining: 7/10 tank
C) Phase 2 rate: 1/10 - 1/15 = 1/30
D) Time: (7/10) / (1/30) = 21 hours, Total = 24 hours

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Phase 1: 3 hours fills 3/10 tank. Remaining = 7/10. Phase 2: net rate = 1/30 per hour, takes 21 hours. Total = 24 hours. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 902:** Alternate pipes: A fills 1/8/hr (works 4 hrs), B fills 1/10/hr (works 5 hrs), repeat. When full?
**Options:**
A) Per cycle: 4/8 + 5/10 = 1/2 + 1/2 = 1 tank (exactly fills in one cycle!)
B) Time = 9 hours per cycle, so fills in 9 hours
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Per cycle: A fills 1/2, B fills 1/2, total = 1 tank. Time per cycle = 9 hours, so fills in exactly 9 hours (one cycle). Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 903:** Multiple drains problem: Tank has inlet 1/6/hr, outlet 1 (1/10), outlet 2 (1/15). Net?
**Options:**
A) Net = 1/6 - 1/10 - 1/15 = 10/60 - 6/60 - 4/60 = 0
B) Tank fills at ZERO rate, never fills!
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Net rate = 0 (inlet equals total drain rate), so tank never fills. This demonstrates critical balance point where inlet exactly matches drain capacity. Both A and B correctly identify the outcome.

---

**Question 904:** Cistern with pump failure: Inlet 1/8, outlet 1/12, pump (adds 1/20). All work together. Real rate?
**Options:**
A) Net = 1/8 + 1/20 - 1/12 = 15/120 + 6/120 - 10/120 = 11/120
B) Time = 120/11 ‚âà 10.9 hours
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Net rate = 11/120 per hour (inlet + pump - outlet), so time ‚âà 10.9 hours. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 905:** INTERVIEW: Real pool scenario. Two fill pipes (different rates), one drain (constant), one seasonal leak. Variables?
**Options:**
A) Total 4+ flow rates
B) Sequence matters (when drain opens, when leak appears)
C) Need to clarify all timing
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Complex scenario with multiple variables: 4+ flow rates, sequence matters (timing of drain and leak), and all timing must be clarified. This demonstrates real-world complexity requiring systematic analysis. All statements are correct.

---

**Question 906:** Pipeline capacity bottleneck: Inlet 1/5/hr, but pipe limits to 1/8/hr. Actual fill rate?
**Options:**
A) Limited by pipe capacity 1/8/hr
B) Time = 8 hours (ignoring inlet's potential)
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Actual fill rate is limited by pipe capacity (1/8/hr), not inlet potential (1/5/hr). Time = 8 hours. This demonstrates bottleneck concept. Both A and B are correct.

---

**Question 907:** Tank overflow prevention: Inlet 1/6/hr, max capacity 100L, minimum drain 1/10/hr (safety). Design problem?
**Options:**
A) Net = 1/6 - 1/10 = 1/15/hr
B) Still fills positive (safe to design)
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Net rate = 1/15/hr (positive), so tank fills safely. Design is safe with positive net rate. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 908:** Maintenance downtime: Normally fills 8 hours. Maintenance hour 4, pipe stops 30 min. New time?
**Options:**
A) Phase 1: 4 hours at 1/8 = 1/2 tank
B) Remaining: 1/2 tank
C) Phase 2: 0.5 hours stopped, then resume = (1/2) / (1/8) = 4 hours more
D) Total = 8.5 hours (extra 0.5 from downtime)

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Phase 1: 1/2 tank filled in 4 hours. Phase 2: 0.5 hours downtime, then remaining 1/2 takes 4 hours. Total = 8.5 hours (0.5 hours extra from downtime). All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 909:** Weather-dependent: Inlet 1/6 (constant), seasonal evaporation 1/20 (summer only). Fill time varies summer vs. winter?
**Options:**
A) Winter: 1/6 = 6 hours
B) Summer: 1/6 - 1/20 = 7/60 = 60/7 ‚âà 8.57 hours
C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Winter: net rate = 1/6, time = 6 hours. Summer: net rate = 7/60, time ‚âà 8.57 hours. Seasonal variation affects fill time. Both calculations are correct.

---

**Question 910:** INTERVIEW: Design resilience. If one pipe fails mid-operation, what's contingency?
**Options:**
A) Must identify critical pipes vs. redundant
B) Single points of failure risk
C) Design with buffer capacity
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Problem Solving
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Design resilience requires: identifying critical vs. redundant pipes, understanding single points of failure risk, and designing with buffer capacity. This demonstrates engineering thinking. All statements are correct.

---

**Question 911:** Crew + water system: 10 workers complete in 20 days need water support. Two fill pipes: 1/12 & 1/15/hr, drain 1/20/hr. Can support 24-day project if needs 1 tank/day?
**Options:**
A) Water net rate = 1/12 + 1/15 - 1/20 = 5/60 + 4/60 - 3/60 = 1/15/hr
B) Fills tank (needed 1/day = 1/24/hr demand)
C) Yes, water system sufficient
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Water net rate = 1/15/hr = 1.6 tanks/day. Demand = 1 tank/day. Since supply (1.6) > demand (1), water system is sufficient. All calculations are correct.

---

**Question 912:** Phased project with changing water demand: Phase 1 (5d, low demand), Phase 2 (10d, high demand). Design pipe capacity?
**Options:**
A) Size pipes for Phase 2 peak demand
B) Oversized for Phase 1 (inefficient) or use pump switches
C) Both A and B
D) All above show design trade-offs

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Problem Solving
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Design options: size for peak demand (oversized for Phase 1) or use variable capacity (pump switches). Both approaches have trade-offs between efficiency and flexibility. All statements demonstrate design thinking.

---

**Question 913:** Integration: Workers and pipes both use rate concepts. Similarity?
**Options:**
A) Both measured per unit time
B) Combined rates sum in both cases
C) Worker-days = Pipe-hours (same concept)
D) All show conceptual similarity

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Integration
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Workers and pipes both use rate concepts (per unit time), combined rates sum, and worker-days = pipe-hours analogy applies. All statements demonstrate conceptual similarity.

---

**Question 914:** Complex pipes: Multiple inlets, drains, with timing variations. Approach?
**Options:**
A) Break into phases by timing
B) Calculate net rate per phase
C) Sum phase times
D) All above: Break into phases, calculate net rate per phase, sum phase times

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Problem Solving
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Systematic approach: break into phases by timing, calculate net rate per phase, then sum phase times. This handles complex scenarios with multiple variables. All steps are correct.

---

**Question 915:** Pipe efficiency: Can pipe "efficiency" change like worker efficiency?

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time & Work

**Day:** 4

**Question 933:** Multiple drains problem: Tank has inlet 1/6/hr, outlet 1 (1/10), outlet 2 (1/15). Net?

C) Both A and B
D) All above

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time & Work
**Week:** 4
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Net rate = 0 (inlet equals total drain rate), so tank never fills. This demonstrates critical balance point. Both A and B correctly identify the outcome.

**Question 1001:** Speed fundamentally a RATE like work rate from Week 4?
**Options:**
A) Both measure output per unit time
B) Distance to speed as work to work rate
C) Both follow D=S√óT or W=R√óT
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Speed = distance/time, Rate = work/time. Mathematical parallel transfers all Week 4 insights. Both measure output per unit time and follow similar formulas (D=S√óT, W=R√óT). All statements are correct.

---

**Question 1002:** For fixed distance D, which TRUE?
**Options:**
A) Speed and time directly proportional
B) Speed and time inversely proportional
C) Time = Distance/Speed
D) B and C same

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** T = D/S. If distance fixed, speed ‚Üë ‚Üí time ‚Üì (inverse). Speed doubles ‚Üí time halves. Both B and C correctly describe the inverse relationship.

---

**Question 1003:** Car A 150 km in 3h. Car B 200 km in 4h. Which FASTER?

D) Cannot determine

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Both 150/3 = 50 kmh and 200/4 = 50 kmh. Speed = D/T standardizes comparison. Both cars have the same speed.

**Question 1004:** 90 kmh to m/s equals:

D) Cannot convert

**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** kmh ‚Üí m/s: √ó 5/18. Why? 1km/h = 1000m/3600s = 5/18 m/s. Check: 90 √ó 5/18 = 25 m/s ‚úì

**Question 1010:** INTERVIEW: "Why is average speed NOT simple average of segment speeds?"
**Options:**
A) Speeds at different times
B) Times in segments differ; speed TIME-WEIGHTED
C) Ratio y/x remains constant
D) All contribute

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Even equal distances, if times differ (from different speeds), average pulled toward slower speeds dominating time. Time-weighting is fundamental.

Wait recalc: if B starts at position 200 (ahead), after 10h B is at 200+800=1000. A starts at 0, after 10h at 1000. They meet! ‚úì

**Question 1030:** INTERVIEW: "In same-direction motion, why is relative speed the difference, not sum?"

**Explanation:** Same direction: only faster object reduces gap. Relative speed = difference. Opposite: both reduce gap, speeds add.

**Difficulty:** Medium

**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Combined speed = 22 kmh. Time = 1/22 hours ‚âà 2.7 minutes.

**Question 1040:** INTERVIEW: "Why speeds ADD when moving toward each other, but SUBTRACT same direction?"

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** TOWARD: Both reduce distance at combined rate. SAME: Only faster reduces gap. This generalizes all motion.

**Question 1042:** ERROR: "Speed doubled, so time also doubled"
**Options:**
A) True, both increase together
B) False, INVERSE: time HALVES
C) Depends on distance
D) Cannot compare

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 1
**Explanation:** Fixed distance: T = D/S. If S doubles, T = D/2S = T/2 (halved). INVERSE relationship.

**Day:** 1

**Question 1070:** INTERVIEW: "Explain why harmonic mean applies for equal distance segments"

**Question 1084:** Train 60 kmh must stop in 200 m uniform deceleration. Time to stop?
**Options:**
A) 200m = avg speed √ó t. Avg 30 kmh = 8.33 m/s. t = 200/8.33 = 24s
B) 24 seconds correct
C) Cannot determine
D) Distance wrong

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 2
**Explanation:** Distance = (initial+final)/2 √ó time. 200 = 8.33 √ó t ‚Üí t = 24s.

---

**Question 1085:** Object accelerates uniformly 0‚Üí50 m/s in 10 seconds. Distance and average speed?

B) Average speed 25 m/s (avg of 0 and 50)
C) Both correct
D) Cannot determine

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 2
**Explanation:** Uniform acceleration: distance = avg velocity √ó time = 25 √ó 10 = 250 m.

**Question 1086:** Deceleration problem: Initial 80 kmh, final 20 kmh, distance 500 m. Time?

**Question 1087:** Velocity changes from 0 to V in time t. Distance formula for uniform acceleration?

A) D = V √ó t (wrong, ignores acceleration)

D) B and C same

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 2
**Explanation:** Uniform acceleration from rest: average velocity = V/2. Distance = Vt/2.

**Question 1088:** Object speed = 10 + 2t (linear acceleration, v in m/s, t in seconds). Distance in 5 seconds?

**Question 1089:** Uniform acceleration: distance in first 2s is 10 m. Distance in next 2s (t=2 to t=4)?

**Question 1090:** INTERVIEW: "Why does distance = average velocity √ó time work for any acceleration profile?"

**Question 1097:** VERIFY: Average speed after 100 km journey at 50 kmh average. Does it ALWAYS take 2 hours?

D) B correct

**Question 1098:** Given speed profile with multiple segments (mixed time/distance formats). How to verify total?

A) Sum individual distances = total distance
B) Sum individual times = total time
C) Total D / Total T = average speed
D) All above for complete verification

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 2
**Explanation:** Three-layer verification: distances, times, and average speed formula all consistent.

---

**Question 1099:** INTERVIEW: "Why is average speed NOT simply the middle speed of a multi-segment journey?"
**Options:**
A) Middle speed ignores time allocation
B) Average weighted by TIME, not distance
C) Time-weighting fundamental
D) All

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 2
**Explanation:** Speed is distance/time. Average = total D / total T, NOT average of speeds. Time-weighting ensures correct formula.

---

**Question 1100:** FINAL VERIFICATION: Speed profile 50 kmh for 2h, stop 1h, 70 kmh for 2h. Average for entire 5-hour period?
**Options:**
A) Moving distance: 100 + 140 = 240 km
B) Total elapsed: 5h. Average 240/5 = 48 kmh with stops included
C) Moving avg: 240/4 = 60 kmh
D) B and C both correct, different interpretations

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 2
**Explanation:** Average depends on what's included: with stops = 48 kmh, pure moving = 60 kmh. Clarity essential in real-world applications.

## DAY 3: TRAINS & RELATIVE SPEED (Q1101-Q1150)

**Question 1101:** Train A 100 kmh passes stationary platform. Time to pass 150 m platform?
**Options:**
A) Platform length = 150 m = 0.15 km. Time = 0.15 / 100 = 0.0015h = 5.4 seconds
B) 5.4 seconds correct
C) Cannot determine
D) Time wrong

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Train must travel platform length = 0.15 km. Time = distance / speed = 5.4s.

---

**Question 1102:** Train length 100 m, speed 90 kmh passes platform 50 m long. Time to completely pass?
**Options:**
A) Total distance = train + platform = 150 m = 0.15 km. Time = 0.15 / 90 kmh = 6 seconds
B) 6 seconds correct
C) Cannot determine
D) Time wrong

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** When train passes platform, total distance = train length + platform length.

---

**Question 1103:** Train A 80 kmh behind Train B 60 kmh (same track). Time for A to catch B if A is 40 km behind?

C) Cannot determine
D) Time wrong

**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** A gains on B at 20 kmh. Time for 40 km gap = 2 hours.

---

**Question 1107:** Train A 100 kmh catches Train B 80 kmh (A starts 50 km behind). After meeting, how far does A travel before being 50 km ahead?

**Question 1108:** SAME-DIRECTION LOGIC: If two trains have speeds S‚ÇÅ > S‚ÇÇ, relative speed for catch-up is?

**Question 1136:** Train at 90 kmh is scheduled to arrive station at 3 PM. If speed reduced to 72 kmh, arrives at 4 PM. Distance to station?

D) Cannot determine

**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 3
**Explanation:** Speed reduction causes 1-hour delay over 360 km distance.

## DAY 4: BOATS & RIVER CURRENT (Q1151-Q1200)

**Question 1151:** Boat in still water speed 20 kmh. Current 4 kmh. Effective speed downstream?
**Options:**
A) 20 - 4 = 16 kmh (wrong direction)
B) 20 + 4 = 24 kmh (correct: WITH current)
C) B correct
D) Cannot determine

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Downstream (with current): boat speed + current = 20 + 4 = 24 kmh.

---

**Question 1152:** Boat still water 15 kmh. Current 3 kmh. Effective speed upstream?
**Options:**
A) 15 + 3 = 18 kmh (wrong direction)
B) 15 - 3 = 12 kmh (correct: AGAINST current)
C) B correct
D) Cannot determine

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Upstream (against current): boat speed - current = 15 - 3 = 12 kmh.

---

**Question 1153:** Boat travels 60 km downstream at 20 kmh effective speed. Time taken?

C) Cannot determine
D) Time wrong

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Standard distance/speed formula applies. 60 km / 20 kmh = 3 hours.

---

B) 5 hours correct
C) Cannot determine
D) Time wrong

**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** 60 km / 12 kmh = 5 hours.

---

**Question 1155:** River current speed 2 kmh. Boat in still water 18 kmh. Downstream speed, upstream speed, and ratio?
**Options:**
A) Downstream: 20 kmh. Upstream: 16 kmh. Ratio: 20:16 = 5:4
B) All correct
C) Cannot determine
D) Speeds wrong

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Downstream 18+2=20. Upstream 18-2=16. Ratio 5:4. Shows current effect.

---

**Question 1156:** LOGIC: For a given current and boat speed, which direction is faster?
**Options:**
A) Upstream always faster
B) Downstream always faster
C) Depends on boat
D) Same both ways

**Answer:** B
**Difficulty:** Easy
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Downstream: boat + current (faster). Upstream: boat - current (slower). Current always helps downstream.

---

**Question 1157:** Two boats in still water: A 25 kmh, B 20 kmh. Current 5 kmh. Downstream effective speeds?
**Options:**
A) A: 30 kmh, B: 25 kmh
B) Both affected equally by current
C) A faster by 5 kmh in still water, remains 5 kmh faster downstream
D) All correct

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Current adds equally. Speed difference preserved: 25-20=5 kmh before, 30-25=5 kmh after.

---

**Question 1158:** CURRENT LOGIC: If current 3 kmh and boat in still water 12 kmh, what's the ratio downstream:upstream?
**Options:**
A) 15:9 = 5:3
B) (12+3):(12-3) = 15:9 = 5:3
C) A and B same
D) Cannot determine

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Downstream/Upstream = (B+C)/(B-C) = 15/9 = 5/3 ratio.

---

**Question 1159:** INTERVIEW: "Why is travel speed different upstream vs downstream despite same boat?"
**Options:**
A) Current adds to boat motion downstream
B) Current opposes boat motion upstream
C) Net effect of boat + current varies
D) All above

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Expert
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Current is vector component. Downstream aligned (addition), upstream opposed (subtraction). Same boat, different effective speeds.

---

**Question 1160:** Still water boat speed 30 kmh. Current 6 kmh. For equal time, can boat travel same distance upstream and downstream?

D) All correct

**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Speed difference means for same time, distances differ. Or same distance requires different times.

**Question 1161:** Boat travels 120 km upstream at effective 15 kmh. Return downstream at effective 25 kmh. Total time?

**Question 1162:** Boat covers distance 80 km downstream in 4 hours. Same 80 km upstream in 5 hours. Still water speed and current?

**Difficulty:** Hard
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance

**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** From effective speeds: still water = (downstream+upstream)/2, current = (downstream-upstream)/2.

**Question 1193:** Boat effective speeds: downstream 28 kmh, upstream 20 kmh. Still water and current?
**Options:**
A) Still water: (28+20)/2 = 24 kmh
B) Current: (28-20)/2 = 4 kmh
C) Both correct
D) Cannot determine

**Answer:** C
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Time-Speed-Distance
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 4
**Explanation:** Reverse formulas work for finding still water and current.

---

**Question 1194:** River journey: 150 km downstream at 25 kmh, return 150 km upstream at 15 kmh. Average speed?

D) All correct

**Day:** 4

## DAY 5: INTEGRATION & MASTERY (Q1201-Q1250)

**Question 1201:** Project combines timework (Week 4) and speed-distance (Week 5). Worker travels 50 km at 60 kmh to site, works 8 hours. Total elapsed?
**Options:**
A) Travel: 50/60 = 0.83 hours
B) Work: 8 hours
C) Total: 8.83 hours
D) All correct

**Answer:** D
**Difficulty:** Medium
**Topic:** Integration
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 5
**Explanation:** Integration of travel time and work time. Total elapsed = travel + work.

---

**Question 1202:** Delivery route: 3 stops, distances 20 km, 30 km, 25 km. Speeds 40 kmh, 50 kmh, 45 kmh. Total time?

C) Stop 3: 25/45 = 0.56h

**Topic:** Integration
**Week:** 5
**Day:** 5
**Explanation:** Sum of individual segment times.
